The Relief Committee for Industrial and Commercial Loans Held its Third Meeting Yesterday

The Central News Agency reports that the Ministry of Finance allocated 20 million yuan in national treasury certificates as a guarantee for industrial and commercial loans to provide relief to the industries and business in Shanghai. Cai Zengji and twelve others were appointed as custody committee members to be responsible for the implementation. A meeting was convened yesterday afternoon to discuss the charter and loan regulations to be submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval and implementation. The details are as follows:

Name Changed: After the Establishment of the Ministry of Finance's National Treasury Certificate Custody Committee for Relief of Industry and Commerce, the third meeting was convened. It was decided to change the name of the committee to "Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Loan Committee." The number of committee members remains at twelve without any increase. However, the titles of vice chairman and committee member were abolished and changed to standing committee member. The number of people, including Chairman Cai Zengji, remained at seven.

Meeting Circumstances: Yesterday afternoon, the committee members had lunch together at the Bankers' Club and then held a meeting. The committee members present were Cai Zengji, Wu Xingya, Song ZiLiang, Chen Guangfu, Xi Demao, Qin Runqing, Yu Zuoting, Wang Yansong, Zhang Peishen, and others. Vice Minister Xu Kan of the Ministry of Finance was also present. Chairman Cai Zengji proposed the draft charter of the committee and the loan measures for detailed discussion. The meeting adjourned at around 3:00 PM.

Meeting Results: After the meeting, according to Cai, the meeting decided to submit all the draft charters and detailed rules and regulations to the standing committee for discussion, and then convene a plenary meeting to be approved and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval and implementation. The contents cannot be disclosed to the public for the time being. It was also learned that when loans are issued in the future, industrial and commercial firms will submit collateral for review, and then notify the banks to make loans, with the national treasury certificates allocated by the Ministry of Finance as the second collateral.

The Siamese Overseas Chinese Petition Delegation, the Third Group of Representatives Returns Home. Zheng Haoyu and Two Others Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday, Scheduled to Go to Beijing Within Days to Appeal to the Central Government

The oppression of overseas Chinese by the Siamese government has been increasing without end. Recently, Siamese farmers, facing the threat of economic ruin, had a rice looting incident. Unexpectedly, the Siamese government falsely accused the overseas Chinese of instigating it and arrested nine overseas Chinese and imprisoned them. The overseas Chinese in Siam found this humiliation intolerable and specially appointed a third group of representatives to return to the country to petition. The representatives arrived in Shanghai yesterday. The details learned by the Real Estate Journal reporters are as follows:

Overseas Chinese Representatives Arrive in Shanghai Yesterday

Our people are outraged by the harsh treatment of overseas Chinese by the Siamese government. Siamese rice merchants were greatly alarmed upon hearing this news. The number of unemployed farmers in the country is increasing day by day, so more than ninety farmers went to the agricultural affairs company to request employment (according to the system, Siamese farmers who are willing to cultivate the land can go to the agricultural affairs company to declare to the landlord that they are willing to cultivate a certain amount of land, and then go through the procedures). Because the company could not accommodate their request, it caused a great riot among the farmers, who looted rice. The Siamese authorities sent police to suppress the riot, and the resulting gunfire caused many casualties to the Siamese farmers. Unexpectedly, the Siamese government, taking the incident as the fault of Chinese instigation, suddenly arrested nine overseas Chinese. Our three million overseas Chinese in Siam, finding themselves repeatedly subjected to disasters, decided that it could not be tolerated. They then appointed Zheng Haonan, Li Fubiao and two others to come to Shanghai yesterday, scheduled to go to Beijing within days to appeal to the Central Government, requesting relief.

Telegraph to the Whole Country, Requesting Assistance

The representatives sent out a telegram: "To the Central Party Headquarters of the Kuomintang in Nanjing, the National Government, the Southwest Executive Department of Guangzhou, the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, all newspapers in the country, and civil organizations: The matter of delaying the Chinese issue has lasted more than a month. Our three million overseas Chinese in Siam are in dire straits every day, suffering the unreasonable oppression of this small country. We cry out to the sky, but who feels our pain? Therefore, the entire overseas Chinese community in Siam especially appointed representatives to return home to request the government to strongly negotiate with the Siamese government and to announce the truth to the people of the country. Recently, the Siamese government has shown no intention of modifying these harsh regulations, and has even gone further. We, the overseas Chinese, are alarmed by the danger of future assimilation, and for the sake of implementing our demands, we have once again dispatched Haonan, Fubiao, and others to return home to continue to appeal to the authorities. We earnestly hope that the government will consider the difficulties of the overseas Chinese and continue to negotiate for the overseas Chinese, so as to maintain the feelings of the overseas Chinese and attach importance to the national system. We are deeply grateful and await your orders. Respectfully, the overseas Chinese representatives returning from Siam, Zheng Haonan and Li Fubiao (seal)."

Petition Delegation Returns to Shanghai Today

The petition delegation of all circles in Qihai City to assist the Siamese overseas Chinese, went to Beijing a few days ago to petition the Central Party Headquarters, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, and has now arrived in Beijing. The delegation sent a letter to the Overseas Chinese Federation yesterday, saying: "Our delegation arrived in Beijing at 7:30 AM this morning (i.e., the 16th) and is now staying at Central Hotel Room 336. After a short rest, we will decide to carry out the following tasks tomorrow: (1) Petition the government; (2) Receive the press in Beijing; (3) Send a note to the Siamese Far East Inspection Group. All circles in Beijing have expressed great sympathy to our delegation and intend to support us unanimously. The atmosphere is strong. The inspection group is scheduled to leave Beijing for Shanghai on the 18th (i.e., today). If there is not enough time, we also hope that Shanghai will prepare to launch a large-scale publicity campaign. We look forward to hearing more details from here tomorrow. We wish you success and hard work, the Petition Delegation, June 16."

The NEC held its Standing Committee Meeting Yesterday to Discuss the Next Year's Budget and the Progress of Projects. Meetings will be Held Once a Month in Both Beijing and Shanghai Hereafter.

The National Economic Council convened a standing committee meeting at the residence of Zeng Zhongming on Jarre Avenue yesterday afternoon at around 4:00 PM to discuss the next year's budget and the progress of projects, and adjourned at around 6:40 PM. The details are as follows:

Standing Committee Members Present

The National Economic Council convened a standing committee meeting at the residence of Zeng Zhongming on Jarre Avenue yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM. All four standing committee members, Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, Kong Xiangxi, and Song Ziwen, were present, except for Chairman Jiang, who was unable to attend due to military operations directing the suppression of bandits in Sichuan. Qin Fen, Secretary-General of the NEC, also attended to report on the work situation this year and to take minutes. Liu Ruiheng, Director of the National Health Administration, also attended to contribute opinions on health care. The discussion of the next year's budget and project progress was very detailed, and the meeting adjourned at around 6:40 PM.

Meeting Results

According to President Wang, after the end of the standing committee meeting, the National Economic Council has decided to hold two standing committee meetings per month thereafter, one meeting in Shanghai and one meeting in Nanjing. According to Finance Minister Kong, in addition to the next year's budget, detailed decisions were made regarding the next year's project progress. According to Qin Fen, the resolutions of the standing committee meeting still need to be sorted out and will be released after returning to Beijing.

Qin Fen's Talk

After arriving in Shanghai yesterday morning, Secretary-General Qin Fen of the NEC went to visit NEC standing committee member Song Ziwen to report. He then met with reporters from various newspapers at the NEC's Shanghai office. According to him, the cases discussed at today's (i.e., yesterday's) meeting concerned a report on the expenditures for the 23rd year. The expenses of the association in the 23rd year were reduced compared to the 22nd year. The expenses for the 22nd year for business expenses were 15 million yuan, and water conservancy expenses were 6 million yuan. The expenses for the 23rd year were reduced to 6 million for business expenses and 5 million for water conservancy expenses. The expenses for the 24th year are the same as those for the 23rd year. The 24th year has already been set to begin on July 1st, so the expenses and income for the 23rd year and the budget for the 24th year will be presented for reporting and discussion at this meeting. In terms of work, in addition to reporting on the work situation in the 23rd year, the work situation for the 24th year will also be presented for detailed discussion. The scope of the discussion is (1) highways, (2) water conservancy, (3) agriculture and industry, (4) cotton industry, (5) sericulture, and (6) health care. The detailed situation of this outline of work is yet to be discussed before it can be decided. Regarding the construction of national highways, it is actively underway. The construction of the Sichuan-Hubei, Sichuan-Shaanxi, and Sichuan-Gansu highways is also underway and will soon be opened to traffic one after another. The three highways are not only related to the transportation of Sichuan, Hubei, Shaanxi, and Gansu, but also have a close relationship with the suppression of the remaining bandits in the four provinces. Apart from this, the early completion of the three highways is of great importance to the suppression of the remaining bandits in Sichuan. Regarding the issue of League of Nations technical cooperation, since Haas, the League of Nations technical cooperation liaison officer stationed in China, returned to Geneva, the League of Nations currently has no need to immediately send personnel to be stationed in China. However, technical cooperation will not be reduced because there is no special envoy stationed in China. As for the arrival of technical experts for guidance, they come and go as in the past. Water conservancy experts Nie Yufu, Gu De, and Womodo have all completed their terms and left China to return to Geneva.

Mr. Liao Xianlie's Coffin Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday; Central Representatives Arrive to Greet, Public Memorial Service This Morning Before Transport to Capital for State Burial

A Central News Agency report states that the coffin of revolutionary martyr Mr. Liao Zhongkai arrived in Shanghai at 6:00 AM yesterday and was immediately transferred to a special train car prepared by the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations. A public memorial service will be held at 7:00 AM this morning, after which it will be transported to the capital for a state burial. Details of the arrival of Mr. Liao Xianlie's coffin in Shanghai are as follows:

Special Envoy for Receiving the Coffin Arrives in Shanghai

Mr. Xu Chongqing, the special envoy sent by the Central Government to Guangdong to receive the coffin, arrived in Guangzhou on the 5th of this month. After consulting with the Guangdong authorities and Mr. Liao Xianlie's family to finalize the procedures for transporting the coffin, he departed from Guangzhou on the 13th to transport it to Shanghai. Accompanying him were Madam He Xiangning, Mr. Liao Xianlie's younger brother Liao Enxun, Madam Liao's secretary Zhang Dingyi, and four female servants.

Chinese and Western Detectives Provide Strict Security

At 6:00 AM yesterday morning, the ship arrived at the China Merchants Bureau's central pier. It was fully berthed at approximately 6:20 AM. Chief Inspector Tan of the Municipal Police Bureau, detectives, and Chinese and Western detectives dispatched by the Public Concession Police patrolled the pier and provided strict security. The military band dispatched by the Municipal Police Bureau also welcomed the arrival with mournful music. Also present at the pier to oversee everything were Mr. Li Dachao, the section chief of the Municipal Government's First Section, officials from the Guangdong Native Place Association, and several relatives of the Liao family. All welcoming personnel were also waiting at the pier. Banners welcoming the arrival were displayed by the Central Military Academy, the Guangdong Native Place Association, and others.

More Than 300 People Greet at the Pier

Among those who greeted at the pier were Mr. Chen Shuren, representing the Central Party Headquarters; Mr. Gan Naiguang, representing Chairman Chiang; Central Committee members Mr. and Mrs. Liu Yazi and Chen Di; Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng; all members of the Municipal Party Headquarters; Mr. Yu Kaizhan, a consultant at the Ministry of Industries; Mr. Yu Ming, the director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office; Mr. Cai Jingjun, the director of the Municipal Police Bureau; Mr. Jian Jinglun, the director of the Shanghai Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau; Mr. Qiu Henian of the Trademark Bureau; Mr. Tang Hai'an, the superintendent of the Jianghai Customs; Mr. Li Yuxuan, representing the Guangdong Native Place Association; Liu Qian, Lü Zhe, and Sheng Qunhe, representing all students and staff of the Whampoa Military Academy and the Central Military Academy; and more than 300 relatives and friends of the Liao family.

Representatives Console Madam Liao

After the ship was secured, the representatives boarded the ship to pay their respects to Madam Liao. Madam Liao was resting in the lounge, wearing a black satin cheongsam and a fur-collared overcoat. She appeared unwell and her face was filled with grief. As the representatives and relatives offered their condolences to Madam Liao, tears welled up in her eyes, making the scene extremely sorrowful. She was then assisted off the ship by relatives and briefly sat on the pier. All the welcoming personnel shook hands with Madam Liao and offered their condolences.

Whampoa Students Assist in Carrying the Coffin onto the Vehicle

Mr. Liao Xianlie's coffin was located in the hold of the ship. It was lifted to the pier by a crane. The coffin was placed in a wooden outer coffin, covered with the national flag. A hearse was prepared by the China Funeral Home, but because the wooden outer coffin was too large and the hearse was too small, the wooden outer coffin was temporarily removed. The coffin was wrapped in a red satin quilt, on which were written the words "The Spirit of Martyr Liao Xianlie Will Never Die." It was then carried onto the hearse by more than ten students from the Whampoa Military Academy, including Liu Qian, Lü Zhe, and Sheng Qunhe.

Departure at 7:00 AM to the North Station

At exactly 7:00 AM, the procession departed from the pier. The Municipal Police Bureau's military band led the way, followed by the Boy Scouts, the vehicle carrying Mr. Liao Xianlie's portrait, the hearse, and finally the Liao family relatives. Representatives from all walks of life walked in an orderly manner. The route was protected by Chinese and Western detectives, passing through Broadway Road, Avenue Road, North Sichuan Road, Yu Garden Road, North Henan Road, Baoshan Road, and Xinmin Road to the North Station.

Special Train Parked on Shanghai-Songhu Branch Line

The special train for transporting the coffin was parked on the Shanghai-Songhu branch line at the North Station. It was covered with blue cloth, on which were inscribed the white characters "Special Train for the Coffin of Martyr Liao Zhongkai." One end was decorated with the national flag. A plain-colored archway was erected at the station, and a memorial altar was set up. In front of the altar were wreaths from the Central Executive Committee, the Central Supervisory Committee, the Shanghai Fish Market Preparatory Office of the Ministry of Industries, Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, the United Association of Guangdong Merchants, the Whampoa Alumni Association, Mr. and Mrs. Zhang Fakui and Liu Jingrong, Yu Kaizhan, the Overseas Transportation Department of the Allied Righteousness, and various branches. The arrangement was particularly neat and solemn.

Central Representatives Hold Salutes

After the coffin arrived at the North Station, it was carried onto the train by Whampoa students, and Mr. Liao Xianlie's portrait from the portrait vehicle was placed on the memorial altar. Mr. Xu Chongqing, the Central Government's special envoy for receiving the coffin, Mr. Chen Shuren, representing the Central Government, Mayor Wu, representatives from all walks of life, and relatives of the Liao family paid their highest respects to Mr. Liao Xianlie's portrait. Finally, Madam Liao paid her respects to Mr. Liao Xianlie and thanked the representatives and relatives before departing.

Madam Liao Suffers from Grief and Illness

After the ceremony, a reporter from the Central News Agency offered condolences to Madam He Xiangning and inquired about her well-being. She stated that she had been suffering from illness recently. Traveling from Guangzhou to Shanghai had worsened her condition due to sea sickness. Therefore, after escorting the coffin to the capital for the state burial, she would return to Shanghai in approximately three days to rest and seek treatment for her chronic ailments.

Public Memorial Service by All Circles at 7:00 AM This Morning

At 7:00 AM this morning, the municipal party and government organs and all circles of the city will hold a public memorial service in front of Mr. Liao Xianlie's coffin on the Shanghai-Songhu branch line at the North Station. All organs and groups will send representatives to participate. Mayor Wu Tiecheng will preside over the ceremony. The memorial pavilion has already been set up, with a bamboo cloth banner hanging in front, inscribed with the words "Public Memorial Service by All Circles in Shanghai for the State Burial of Martyr Liao Zhongkai." At 8:00 AM, the coffin car will be attached to the Shanghai-Nanjing special express train to the capital. Madam Liao and Mr. Xu Chongqing will accompany the train to the capital.

Madam Liao Speaks of Hoping Compatriots

Madam He Xiangning met with a reporter from the National News Agency on the ship. Madam He's hair was already gray, her face showed grief, and she appeared physically weak. When she met with the reporter, she said with a trembling voice, "This time, the Central Government is transporting Mr. Liao's coffin from Guangdong to the capital to be buried in the Mausoleum of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen. Recalling that Mr. Liao devoted his life to the revolution, following Dr. Sun Yat-Sen's advocacy, being unyielding and working hard for the revolution, he sacrificed himself for this cause. Almost ten years have passed since Mr. Liao's martyrdom, and yet the revolution has not yet succeeded and the national crisis remains. Although I am filled with boundless grief, I still hope that all comrades and compatriots throughout the country will continue Mr. Liao's legacy, complete the revolution, restore the nation, and hope that all the world's small and weak nations will work together." Madam He also told the reporter that she would return to Shanghai in two or three days after escorting Mr. Liao's coffin to the capital.

Radio Stations Report History

In addition to notifying all circles to send representatives to participate in the welcoming of the coffin and the public memorial service, the Municipal Party Headquarters has instructed the Shanghai Wireless Radio Broadcasting Association to direct all radio stations in the city to broadcast reports on the history of Mr. Liao Xianlie's involvement in the revolutionary cause yesterday and today, in order to promote the spirit of revolutionary martyrs' struggle to the citizens for emulation. The Municipal Party Headquarters has also printed a proclamation to comrades and compatriots, detailing Mr. Liao's revolutionary deeds.

China Farmers Bank to Launch Chattel Mortgage Loans, Entering Into Contracts With Pawnshops in Various Places to Provide Cash, Offering Low-Interest Loans to Farmers to Regulate Rural Finance

Xinxin News Agency reports that the China Farmers Bank, in order to regulate rural finance, has entered into contracts with pawnshops in various places, under which the bank provides cash to the pawnshops, which then offer low-interest loans to farmers to provide general relief. Because there are no banks or money shops established in rural areas of China, the only place for farmers to borrow money is to mortgage items at pawnshops in various towns and villages, with interest rates generally at two percent. In recent years, due to rural bankruptcy, farmers have been unable to redeem their mortgaged items, resulting in the closure of pawnshops, making it even more difficult for farmers to borrow money. In light of this situation, the bank has specially launched chattel mortgage loans to provide relief to farmers. The bank's total loan budget for this year is 11.25 million yuan, an increase of 2.76 million yuan compared to last year. The scope of lending mainly focuses on cooperative loans, farmers' chattel mortgages, and cotton industry improvement loans.

Records of Contemporary Figures' Whereabouts

Tang Youren, Cai Yuanpei, Chuan Rulin, Liu Ruiheng, Liu Weizhi, Chu Minyi, and others took the night express train to the capital yesterday.

American Economic Mission Hosts Banquet for All Circles Last Night; Six Members Return to the US by Ship This Morning; The Rest to Depart on the Next Sailing; Guo Bingwen and Zhang Gongquan Deliver Sincere Speeches

The American Economic Mission, which came to China for inspection, has completed its work. Six members of the mission took the Dollar Steamship Lines' President Coolidge to return to the US this morning. Last night, the mission leader, Mr. Forbes, held a banquet at the International Hotel to thank the entire reception committee and Sino-American circles in the city. The Central News Agency reporter has compiled the details as follows:

Departing for the United States Today

The mission's inspection in China has lasted nearly two months and has now been completed. Mission leader Forbes, Deputy Leader Carroll, and members Lame, Wickham, Harkins, and Landman departed last night after the farewell banquet, taking company launches at 12:00 AM and 1:45 AM respectively to board the President Coolidge. All members of the reception committee went to the dock to see them off and presented many flower baskets. Wang Yutai Tea House also prepared many tins of finely packaged tea to give to the mission members. The President Coolidge is scheduled to weigh anchor at 7:30 AM this morning. Mission members Rogers, Bispe, and Combbell will return on the next sailing due to personal matters. It is reported that the mission will still be studying the materials obtained during this inspection on the ship.

Hosting a Banquet for All Circles Last Night

At 8:00 PM last night, the mission held a banquet for the entire reception committee and Sino-American circles at the International Hotel. In addition to all the members of the host side, those present included Wu Tiecheng, Zhang Gongquan, Chen Zheqing, Guo Bingwen, Xu Xinliu, He Bingxian, Wang Boqi, Cao Yunxiang, Pan Guangjiong, He Dekui, Wang Xiaolai, Jin Lüqin, Xia Xiaofang, Miao Zhongxiu, Xu Shanxiang, Zhang Xianglin, Wen Yuqing, Yang Guanghuo, Li Dachao, Pan Gongzhan, Cai Zengji, Xu Peihuang, Yang Hu, Ma Yinchu, Wu Liande, Wu Yunzhai, Xi Demao, Shen Shuyu, Tang Baoshu, Xi Jiming, Lu Ganchen, Li Quanshi, Ma Yinliang, He Xiya, and the commander of the US forces stationed in Shanghai, An Hai, US Consul General Ke Yinhai, and Arnold of the Sino-American Trade Association. There were over 200 people in total. After the meal, dancing was held. Afterwards, the mission members organized their luggage. The reception staff gathered on the second floor and accompanied them to the ship one after another.

Forbes Delivers Speech

At the banquet, the leader of the American Economic Mission, Forbes, stood up and delivered a speech, saying briefly that he was deeply grateful for the companionship and kindly prepared this simple meal in return for the hospitality. He hoped that they would continue to interact with each other to promote the development of Sino-American trade. During the two months of this trip, he deeply felt that China was rich in resources, and that various facilities, such as highways, civil aviation, and construction, were thriving, and that the future development was truly within reach. He and his colleagues will board the ship tonight to return to their country, and will bring back the results of the observation and the opinions exchanged with all circles in China to contribute to the government and people of their country, so as to provide a basis for the development of Sino-American trade. He then raised his glass to thank them for their warm hospitality and wished all those present good health.

Guo Bingwen Responds

Then Dr. Guo Bingwen, the vice chairman of the reception committee, responded, "Gentlemen of the American Mission, I would like to say a few words on behalf of the reception committee and all the organizations present, in response to your kindness. I must first thank you for the grand reception this evening. I heard the leader of the mission praise the thoughtfulness of our reception and the various conveniences in terms of investigation, considering it our obligation in terms of friendship. As Confucius said, 'Is it not delightful to have friends coming from distant quarters?' Therefore, our hope is to fulfill our duty as hosts as much as possible, so that the mission can have all kinds of conveniences during their stay in China, in other words, to assist the mission in achieving the goal of increasing trade between China and the United States. Gentlemen of the Mission, it is a great honor for the people of our country to get to know you during your visit to China. The seriousness of your investigation in China, the magnanimous attitude, the humility in receiving people, and the emphasis on facts are deeply felt by all people in our country. We have no need to deny that our country's trade and economic facilities have not been as good as we would like. And the various issues discussed with your country in the past may not be completely agreed upon by each other, but we have at least achieved one goal, that is, mutual understanding and humbly accepting each other's views. Before all the Chinese and foreign guests, I must explain one thing. The problem of trade, no matter how important it is, is only one of the problems of increasing friendship between the two countries. Seeing the officials of your country present, we can know how rapid the increase of diplomatic relations between the two countries is. Recalling the educators, doctors, etc. of your country, we can know the greatness of their contribution to our country's education, medicine and religion. The students studying in the United States present tonight can be associated with the large number of Chinese students studying in American universities every year. Therefore, we believe that in politics, culture, and commerce, etc., it is sufficient to illustrate that the relationship between China and the United States for more than a century and a half has been purely friendly and cordial, and the national friendship is pure, which is justified. Governor Forbes, I recall that you once said that at any banquet in China, the people of our country never fail to mention the silver problem. It can be said that the opinions of the people of our country on the silver problem have been contributed to you as much as possible. I can make an exception tonight and no longer raise this issue. However, there is one point that can be used to help you think, that is, the commercial counselor of your country, Mr. Arnold, once said that a Chinese friend of his asked him to answer the question of how to dispose of the large amount of silver purchased by the United States. Mr. Ann replied with a smile, 'The United States has many places where dark clouds are scattered, and the white light of silver will be used to dispel them.' Gentlemen, there are also many places in our country where dark clouds are scattered, but there are also many places where white light is scattered, in other words, the hope for our country's future is also unlimited. Since the enemy country has made considerable efforts in various political foundations, economic construction, and social transformation in recent years, if we can give it time, our country is convinced that various difficulties will be gradually eliminated, and a stable and prosperous new China will be established. The gentlemen also expressed optimism after returning from the interior, although the facts are like this, but the encouragement of the gentlemen is enough to make us work hard. However, the people of our country also deeply know that the difficulties ahead of our country are heavy, and the responsibility is also very heavy, and only we ourselves can bear this responsibility. The famous saying that God helps those who help themselves is what we really believe in. However, we always welcome and accept the good intentions and assistance of friendly countries, especially the United States, because your country is most interested in the safety of our country, and there are reasons for cooperation between the two countries. Your country is rich in machinery, industrial knowledge, and capital, and our country is rich in natural resources and manpower, which is the best place for foreign investment. Therefore, I firmly believe that cooperation between the two countries will be mutually beneficial. Gentlemen, I must bring this to an end. In a few hours, our guests will leave here, which is very appropriate. The purpose of their coming to China is very large, and they will be busy with the report of the investigation afterwards. We deeply regret that we cannot keep you here any longer, but we sincerely hope that your work can be very successful. Finally, I would like to express our greatest respect to the Sino-American Trade Association and the American Foreign Trade Association, which sponsored your visit to China. The various groups in our country are always ready to work hard to cooperate. I sincerely hope that in the near future, the enemy country can also organize a Chinese mission to the United States to respond to the grand intention of your visit to China and to promote the further increase of the friendly relations between the two countries. I would like to represent the entire reception committee and the various groups in Shanghai to wish you a safe journey and all the best."

Zhang Gongquan's Speech of Thanks

Finally, Zhang Gongquan, the director of the reception committee, responded, "Governor Forbes, Admiral An Hai, Consul General Ke Yinhai, Mayor Wu, and all of you ladies and gentlemen, I recall that in mid-April, I had the honor of attending the welcome to the American Economic Mission to China, and time flies, and tonight I have to bid farewell to you. I have been traveling in Beiping for a month, and I am very happy to be able to return to my hometown before you leave China. The fact that the American mission has traveled all over the world for the benefit of trade between the two countries for nearly two months and has achieved so much is unprecedented. This is to be congratulated on the noble mission. As for the reception committee, it is an honor to be able to cooperate and share all the optimistic images of the noble mission during the trip and investigation of the noble mission. Therefore, I dare to tell you that it is a pleasure to be able to do my best as a host. Now that we are about to part, I can't help but feel lost. Dr. Guo Bingwen has said it very clearly, and I don't want to say too much. I have paid close attention to the actions and all the actions of the responsible mission, and I am glad to know that every time you gather with the people of the country, you have a spirit of friendship. The fact that you can see all aspects of China's situation with the eyes of a critic will be a faithful report to your government and people after you return to your country. If you want to understand China's problems, in addition to the development you have witnessed, please do not forget the background, and the whole review of all of China's problems is the only way. When we try to solve this problem, we always feel that factors that have nothing to do with the real argument cannot be separated. Specifically, the way to increase foreign trade depends on whether the factors related to the economic and political nature can be reviewed in detail. 'What is the result of the mission?' This is what all related parties want to ask. My answer is that we do not expect immediate results, but we feel that long-term contact and the increase of friendship have brought closer understanding and goodwill between the people of the two countries. This is the best and most lasting of all results. There are many people from friendly countries who come to China and express their willingness to help China, but I hope that the noble mission will not be troubled by this. We only hope that you will understand, which is the basis for all cooperation. It is a great honor for us to have the opportunity to meet with the members of the noble mission, and it is regrettable that we have to say goodbye to you now."

Yesterday's General Meeting of All Crew Members: Opposing Salary Cuts by Shipping Companies; Declaration Issued to the Government

The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association, citing the decline of the shipping industry, requested the Central Government to issue 10 million yuan in shipping bonds. It decided to reduce the salaries of all crew members earning 15 yuan or more by 20% starting July 1, which triggered strong opposition from all crew members. The Masters’ Association, Marine Engineers' Association, and Ship Radio Officers' Association have been holding meetings for days to discuss countermeasures. Yesterday afternoon, the three groups held a joint meeting and decided on a method of opposition. At that time, it was decided to issue a declaration of resistance to salary cuts by shipping companies and to submit a petition to the Central Government requesting fair handling. The details of this matter are described below.

Crew Members' General Meeting

Yesterday afternoon at 3 PM, all crew members gathered at the Marine Engineers' Association to convene a joint meeting of the Masters’ Association, the Radio Officers' Association. Responsible representatives, including Lin Yi, Di Guixuan, Jun Yu, Jiang Shangtao, and others, were present to discuss the issue of salary cuts by shipping companies starting on July 1. The representatives unanimously expressed their opposition, arguing that the shipping industry was not as declining as the shipping companies claimed, and that the salaries of Chinese crew members were already very low, only about two-fifths of those of foreign crew members, while the cost of living in society was not decreasing. They believed that the salary cut was intended for other purposes. The atmosphere at the meeting was very agitated, and it was decided to issue a declaration. A resolution was passed immediately, and several countermeasures were discussed, which were not announced for the time being. The meeting adjourned at around 5 PM.

Declaration Issued

The declaration was jointly signed by the Marine Engineers' Association, the Masters’ Association, and the Ship Radio Officers' Association. The original text is as follows: "Amidst the North China crisis, with national peril imminent, the crew members, vigilant against foreign aggression reaching its final stage, rely on the nation to unite and not allow the shipping and capital parties to create trouble and disrupt themselves, thus providing opportunities for foreigners. Therefore, in recent years, crew members, although subjected to oppression and feeling deep pain, have endured it silently, without large-scale protests to improve their own interests. This was initially motivated by patriotism, hoping for temporary peace. Unexpectedly, yesterday we received a letter from the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association and a subsequent declaration published in the newspaper, citing the decline in business and deciding at a meeting that from July 1, the monthly salaries of crew members earning 15 yuan or more would be reduced by 20%, and that the government would be asked to issue shipping bonds to rescue shipping companies. Our associations believe that their statements are untrue and that these actions are purposeful, sacrificing the crew members in order to achieve their goals. The means are extremely harsh. Therefore, our associations have jointly discussed and united in opposition, first revealing their inside story, and then refuting their claims to inform the public and clarify right and wrong. Since the National Government established its capital, the rental fees paid for shipping vessels for military use have been calculated according to the tonnage of each vessel, and expenses such as coal, water, and pilotage have been paid in full. This kind of business is far superior to shipping companies carrying cargo on their own. Shipping companies cannot guarantee that each voyage will be fully loaded, but when rented for military use, they are fully paid according to tonnage. Given this income, which is better is obvious. To claim that they are losing rights and serving the government is simply untrue and shows a lack of gratitude. The September 18th Incident, the January 28th Incident, combined with floods and droughts, have superficially affected shipping companies, but examining the internal situation, it is not true that the shipping industry is on the verge of collapse, as the association claims. Let us cite a major example: after the Northeast Incident, with commercial goods decreasing and freight rates falling daily, new ships have sprung up like bamboo shoots after rain, swarming in. Such as Xinpu, Mingxing, Jing'an, Songshan, Yongjia, Shouchang, Haishang, Dalu, Dasheng, Dada, Yuanxing, Kunxing, Huachang, Huaqiang, Xinmaoli, Beian, Muyou, Fuping, Zhongxing, Yixing, Luxing, Daxing No. 1, Xinhongxing, Tianyou, Haihua, Shunfeng, Yuanchang, Minquan, Debao, as well as the Yijiang, Yixing, Qitai, Yichang, and Qichun, Xietan, etc. that are currently being negotiated, roughly totaling about 40 ships. The number is rarely seen, and the flourishing image of the shipping companies' business, is clear for all to see. Facts speak louder than words, and discerning people can see for themselves. Moreover, coal costs account for a large portion of the expenses of a ship, and before September 18th, the price of coal was about ten taels per ton, while from September 18th to the present, the price has been about ten yuan per ton. For a smaller 1,500-ton ship traveling between Shanghai and Tianjin, a round trip requires 100 to 120 tons of coal. The savings from this are about 400 to 600 yuan. And those sailing to South China use Keelung (Taiwan) coal, which costs only seven yuan per ton, or about five yuan at the market price. Therefore, factually speaking, the monthly expenses of a 1,500-ton ship are about 2,500 yuan, and 80% of that is 2,000 yuan. However, the shipping companies have benefited from the disaster, and the savings on coal are enough to offset the salary reduction. As for the financial difficulties and the difficulty in obtaining cash, this is indeed true. However, the various shipping companies have a precedent of owing wages. For example, Sanbei often owes two months' salary, which is well known. Using this as an excuse is weak. Furthermore, the company is a giant in the private shipping industry. At the beginning of its establishment, the captain of the Shengfu ship was paid 550 yuan per month, the chief engineer 400 yuan, the first assistant engineer 150 yuan, the second assistant engineer 100 yuan, and the third assistant engineer 60 yuan. In recent years, the company's crew salaries have not been so high and have long been reduced. However, the company has developed over the years from one ship, Shengfu, to as many as 18 ships, and has even spun off into Hongan and Ningyu companies, with as many as 13 ships. Also, a certain company purchased a ship with tens of thousands of capital and once paid bonuses of up to hundreds of thousands of yuan, exceeding the capital by several times, and now it has expanded to six ships. Therefore, judging by this, there is some doubt about the so-called business failure of the shipping companies. Is the failure to make ends meet due to crew expenses, or is it due to mismanagement? Are there expenses that go beyond the scope of business, and are they blaming the crew for something they didn't do? Furthermore, the shareholders of the various shipping companies receive dividends from business profits, and the staff receive bonuses, but the crew members have never enjoyed this right. Even if the shipping companies are currently suffering from the depression, they do not consider the hardships of the crew members and are willing to impose oppression and unilaterally reduce salaries. Then, why not take into account the overall situation, put oneself in the position of others, and also reduce the passenger and cargo fares by 20% across the board? The shipping companies cannot come up with this plan, clearly seeking private gain. How can they convince people? Furthermore, nationalizing the shipping industry is a plan set by Dr. Sun Yat-sen. After the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which was in debt for tens of millions of yuan, was nationalized, its business has been booming and improving day by day. Then, if the private companies really value transportation and know to ask the government to issue 10 million yuan in bonds, why not fundamentally solve the problem by asking to be nationalized? Because nationalization prevents the shipping companies from profiting from it, reducing a layer of exploitation on all sides, and nationalized shipping cannot do without crew members. The crew members are not likely to play tricks. Fearing that their demands will not be met, they first reduce the crew members' salaries, clearly provoking a storm and causing human-made disasters, sacrificing all the crew members as a tool to coerce the government, while still claiming that crew members losing their jobs, and their livelihood being cut off, will increase social worries. This can truly be called confusing black and white, and turning right and wrong upside down. Our associations have long known that there are many enlightened people in the shipping industry. Are our associations' words reasonable? And those who preside over this decision and give orders, are there any monopolizing attempts to benefit a few people? Someone will be able to distinguish this. Our associations, in order to break the conspiracy and not be used by others, if the national government issues 10 million yuan in shipping bonds, it would be better to nationalize all private shipping. The crew members are willing to serve the government, and all issues can be discussed. If it comes from the association, then our associations dare to be bold and see if all the members of the association can stop sailing. Our associations are a collection of laborers, but we still roughly understand things. We will not bow our heads and surrender immediately after being threatened, and allow ourselves to be slaughtered. In addition to having already decided to submit a separate petition to the government, asking for fair handling, and to unite together to seek resistance, in the event of gradual coercion, no matter what unexpected events occur, the shipping companies shall bear the responsibility. We hereby announce the inside story to the people of the country, hoping for public judgment. China Merchant Marine Masters’ Association, China Marine Engineers' Association, China Ship Radio Officers' Association. Declaration of All Crew Members Opposing Salary Cuts."

Petition to the Central Government

At the same time, representatives of the three groups, on behalf of all crew members, submitted a petition to five places: the Central Government, the Ministry of Transportation, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, the Central Party Headquarters, and the Executive Yuan. Their wording was the same as the declaration, requesting the Central Government not to be misled by the shipping companies' distortion of right and wrong and their confusion of black and white, and asking the government to handle this matter fairly. In the event that the shipping companies are willing to sacrifice crew members in order to obtain the issuance of shipping bonds, they would rather nationalize private shipping to avoid crew members losing their jobs. The petition to the Central Government will be sent out today. Currently, crew members and shipping companies have reached extremes, and the future is quite dangerous.

Ministry of Finance Approves Chamber of Commerce's Request That Stamp Tax Penalties Not Be Revised; Simple Procedures in Summary Court; No Need to Restore Review Committee

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce believes that the stamp tax penalty measures have caused great hardship to merchants and citizens. It sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance on the first of this month, requesting that Article 8 of the inspection rules be revised to alleviate merchants' difficulties. The federation received a reply from the Ministry of Finance yesterday disapproving the request. The federation's telegram and the Ministry of Finance's reply are recorded below:

Chamber of Commerce Telegram: The federation's telegram to the Ministry of Finance stated, "We recently received a telegram from the Tianjin Chamber of Commerce stating, 'Upon investigation, Article 8 of the Ministry of Finance's inspection rules for stamp tax states, 'When violations of the stamp tax law are discovered during inspections, a list of the inspected location, the inspected merchant, the name and number of documents, and the facts should be prepared and sent to the local government for transfer to the judicial authorities for legal review.' In this city, stamp tax cases investigated from the business community are immediately sent to the court by the Finance Bureau in accordance with this law, resulting in repeated litigation burdens, which often cannot be completed for several months. As a result, businesses are abandoned, and closures and bankruptcies are common. This association proposes to restore the stamp tax review committee and revise Article 8 of the inspection rules to comply with public opinion.' Upon investigation, stamp tax penalties are handled by judicial authorities, which indeed causes endless hardship to merchants and citizens. The reasons for the telegram above are reasonable. We respectfully request your ministry to investigate and approve, and to comply with public opinion to revise Article 8 of the inspection rules to alleviate merchants' difficulties.' Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, respectfully kowtows, with seal."

Ministry of Finance Reply: "Telegram received. Based on the telegram's statement regarding the stamp tax penalty and the request to revise Article 8 of the judicial rules to alleviate merchants' difficulties, the telegram has been noted. Upon investigation, this matter was directly reported to the ministry by the Tianjin Chamber of Commerce. At that time, the reply stated, 'Upon investigation, in the past, stamp tax bureaus in various places often imposed harsh and excessive penalties on cases that violated the stamp tax laws. The review committees that were established also often showed bias and favoritism in their reviews. In order to correct long-standing abuses and ensure fairness, the ministry has specifically stipulated that since the stamp tax stamps are sold by the post office, the cases discovered by the municipal and county governments during inspections and by the provincial stamp tax bureaus during inspections must be sent to the local judicial authorities for review. In the judicial authorities' review of these cases, the summary court conducts the trial, and the procedures are quite simple. What litigation burden is there to speak of? Moreover, the establishment of the review committee was originally based on the stamp tax agencies as the main body. Now that the stamp tax bureaus in various places have been abolished, there is no need to restore it. The request should not be discussed.' You should be informed accordingly. This approval."

Accountants' Association Requests to Assist in Supervising Industrial and Commercial Liquidation Matters

Recently, the Ministry of Finance promulgated six measures for supervising liquidation, and supervisors are selected for all banks and money shops that have been closed and are in liquidation to supervise the process. The National Accountants Association believes that this is a timely and effective measure, but has some comments on Articles 2 and 4 of the measures, which have already been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for consideration. Now, the Shanghai Accountants Association, in view of the recent repeated occurrences of industrial and commercial company and firm closures and liquidation events, decided yesterday to submit a request to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, requesting that the example of the Ministry of Finance's supervisory liquidation measures be used to supervise the industrial and commercial liquidation matters in this city, and to forward the request to the Ministry of Industry and instruct the construction departments and social affairs bureaus of all provinces and cities to implement it uniformly. The original request is recorded as follows: "Request to Assist in Supervising Industrial and Commercial Liquidation Matters. We have investigated that our country's merchants and citizens cannot fully understand the laws and regulations, especially the liquidation procedures and regulations, which are complicated and difficult to understand in detail. Therefore, when our members execute liquidation cases, they often encounter difficulties due to merchants adhering to old habits. Although this is a difficulty for accountants in performing their duties, it also greatly deviates from the original intention of the legal system to protect the people. Recently, we read in the newspaper that the Ministry of Finance has stipulated six measures for supervising liquidation, selecting special commissioners to supervise the liquidation matters of various banks and money shops, bringing them into compliance with the regulations, and the effectiveness can be expected. Since there is an example, we propose that your bureau also assist in the liquidation matters of industrial and commercial companies and firms in this city, so that liquidators and liquidation staff can receive the assistance of government supervision, and merchants can understand the responsibility of complying with laws and regulations. We humbly offer our knowledge and hope that it will be adopted, and we respectfully request that it be forwarded to the Ministry of Industry and instruct the construction departments of all provinces and the social affairs bureaus of all cities to implement it uniformly, which would be for the public convenience. Respectfully submitted to Wu, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau."

Jiangsu Provincial Government Orders County Government to Ban Cherishing-Paper Associations; Waste Paper Can Be Used as Raw Material for Papermaking

The Shanghai County Government received instructions from the Jiangsu Provincial Government, based on a report from Ye Yinshan, chairman of the China Paperboard Factory Association, stating, "Our association is organized by paperboard factories across the country. The factories of our members, including Hangzhou Huafeng, Jiaxing Minfeng, Suzhou Huasheng, and Dahua, Tianjin Zhenhua, etc., are all engaged in the machine-made production of various paperboards, and have been approved by the Ministry of Industry and registered. However, waste paper, which is the raw material for making paperboard, is also a major commodity. Each factory has entrusted people to purchase it in metropolitan commercial ports. However, old customs and superstitions have not been eliminated. Cherishing-Paper Associations are still established in various places, carrying baskets on their shoulders to collect and burn waste paper, which reduces the original production of waste paper. The raw materials for papermaking are greatly affected. It is believed that in the past, when people's knowledge was not developed, they thought that waste paper was combustible, throwing ash into the sea, and could not be re-made into paper, which would desecrate the relics of sages and virtuous men. Now that the times are enlightened, such backward thinking should not be allowed to exist. Moreover, if waste paper is sold to factories to be used as raw material for papermaking, factories can make waste useful and reduce the purchase of imported raw materials. On the other hand, it can also be used to make money and supplement livelihood. However, Cherishing-Paper Associations hire workers to collect and burn waste paper, which still consumes wages. The result is the waste of natural resources. Comparing the two, it seems to have a great relationship with the problem of people's livelihood and economy. One gain and one loss cannot be counted with reason. For this reason, we submit a document and request your review and approval to instruct all subordinate units to ban the original Cherishing-Paper Associations, to cherish material resources and eliminate bad desires, which would be for the public convenience, etc. Based on this, in addition to approval, the county magistrate is ordered to comply with the above-mentioned matters."

Jiande Bank Case Announced Yesterday; Chai Chuangui et al. Fined

Jiande Bank went bankrupt, and all the directors and general manager Chai Chuangui et al. were sued by more than ten creditors, including Wei Haijiang et al., for crimes such as embezzlement and fraud. Bandit Fears Punishment, Hangs Himself; Corpse Examined Yesterday

The bandit Chen Gaofu, age 42, from Jiangbei, gathered more than ten accomplices on the night of April 15th of this year in Yaojing Town, Songjiang, and kidnapped Lu Fushan, a farmer from the area, hiding him in a small boat in the Zhangjiagang River in Shanghai. He sent a letter to the family, demanding 15,000 yuan in foreign currency for ransom. He negotiated the ransom twice in Shanghai, but the matter was not kept secret. Detectives from the Xinzha Police Station in both the Chinese and foreign concessions arrested Chen and 14 other male and female bandits, and rescued the hostage. The next morning, they were escorted to the First Special District Local Court and detained for seven days. All these details have been reported in the newspapers. The police, having learned that Chen Gaofu was the ringleader, also kept him in a separate cell. Unexpectedly, fearing punishment, at 11:30 AM the day after the interrogation, he tore his pants into strips and made a rope, which he tied to a water faucet next to his cell and hanged himself. A western policeman named Mei Yin discovered him while on duty, immediately tried to take him down and attempted artificial respiration, but to no avail. He was then sent to a nearby hospital, but it was too late. He died en route, and the body was transferred to the coroner's office on Avenue Foch. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor specially appointed by the First Special District, accompanied by forensic doctors Wei and Zhang, court clerk Wang Zuyi, and others, arrived at the office to examine the body. Mei Yin, a western policeman, explained the situation, stating that he had seen the deceased peacefully sleeping in his cell at 11:00 AM that morning, but half an hour later, he was discovered to have hanged himself. Judge Guo then ruled that the deceased Chen Gaofu, a male, had indeed committed suicide by hanging, and the body was handed over to the Pushan Mountain Villa for burial.

Contracting Dining Car, Cheating Money; Bai Hongxun Sentenced; Imprisonment for One Year and Six Months; Fined Four Hundred Yuan

Bai Hongxun, a resident of No. 20 Daodeli, Baylor Road, in the French Concession, from Gaoyou, worked as a lawyer in Shanghai. In August of last year, he falsely claimed to be arranging contracts for dining cars, tea rooms, and vendors on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway. He successively took 1,800 yuan from Jiang Youtang, a native of Ningbo residing at No. 21 Jingdeli, Shishan Road, Zhabei, and Feng Yishen, a native of Nantong, as "arrangement fees," issuing receipts. Later, Jiang and others inquired at the Railway Bureau after a long delay without receiving any news, and discovered that Bai had committed fraud under a false name. The Railway Bureau's police reported the case, and on April 23rd of last year, detectives arrested Bai and escorted him to the Second Special Court. The Police Department's lawyer prosecuted him for fraud under Article 36 of the Criminal Law. The victims also filed an incidental private lawsuit, seeking to recover the defrauded funds. These details have been reported in previous newspapers. The case has now been concluded after interrogation. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Qiu HuanYing presided over the Eighth Criminal Court and sentenced Bai Hongxun to one year and six months of imprisonment for continuously and jointly defrauding others into handing over their property with the intent of illegally possessing it, and fined him 400 yuan. He was also ordered to compensate Jiang Youtang and others 1,800 yuan. During the appeal period, he was allowed to be released on a 1,000 yuan surety to guarantee his appearance when summoned. If no surety was provided, he would be returned to custody. Bai immediately declared his dissatisfaction and wished to appeal. The court granted his request, and the bailiffs took Bai down and returned him to the detention center.

After Li Pengxian's Death; Inheritance Causes Trouble

Li's Eldest Son Sells Farmland; Family Members Request Confirmation of Invalidity

Li Pengxian, a native of Ningbo, was a prominent figure in the pawnshop and banking industries. Later, due to business downturns, the businesses he ran were closed down early. Li had two sons and two daughters. The eldest son was Yisheng, and the second son was Yusheng. Zeng Duo had married early. Yisheng established Yuchang Hardware Store on Ningbo Road, and Yusheng established Dasheng Printing and Silk Factory in Shanghai and Ningbo. The two daughters were also married. In addition to his wife, Sun, with whom he had a daughter, Yusheng also took Shi Zhongde, a woman from Suzhou, as a concubine. Shi gave birth to a son named Chenghao, who is now fifteen years old. Recently, Li Pengxian passed away due to illness. His second son, Yusheng, also died about a month after Pengxian's death (January 27th of this year, according to the lunar calendar). Li Pengxian's estate has always been divided. Yisheng received it. At the end of last month, Li Yisheng suddenly sold a portion of the estate, namely five fen one li and seven hao of farmland located at No. 361, Zizhi, Gao Xihuan household, 27 Bao, 11 Tu, Meiyuan Road, Zhabei, for 3,800 yuan. Although his nephew Chenghao co-signed the contract at the time, Chenghao's mother, Shi Zhongde, later claimed that Chenghao's signature was obtained under duress, and the sales contract did not bear the names of the uncle and nephew. She filed a lawsuit to confirm that the contract was invalid, and also published a statement opposing it. In the civil court of the First Special District Court, Judge Shen Hong of the First Special Court opened the Sixth Criminal Court yesterday afternoon for questioning. According to Li Shi, he explained the situation at the time. Li Yisheng was absent, but lawyer Wang Chuanbi appeared in court, stating that the plaintiff Li Chenghao and his legal representative Shi were both present at the time of signing. However, the case is a family dispute, and mediation is currently underway, with the possibility of a settlement. Judge Shen reviewed the statements and ordered a postponement for further questioning.

The Shanghai Municipal Security Bureau and the Municipal Public Security Bureau recently cracked down on a counterfeit banknote manufacturing operation at No. 126 Hepingfang, Baoshan Road, Zhabei, seizing more than 100,000 yuan in counterfeit banknotes and detaining more than 20 suspects. Economic Expert Xu Peikun Talks; Our Country Should Not Abandon Silver Standard; Economic Decline and Abandonment is Self-Disturbance; Currency Research Should Adopt Strengths

Xu Peikun, director of the Social and Economic Survey Institute of the National Economic Committee, gave an important speech to the Dagongshe reporter yesterday about why our country should not abandon the silver standard. The record is as follows,

Silver Standard System; No Need to Abolish

Xu first stated that our country has used the silver standard system for hundreds of years, and there has been no major harm. Most economic scholars, seeing that European and American countries have adopted the gold standard system and the national economy is gradually on track, advocate abandoning the silver standard and adopting other standards in response to the needs of the times. However, in terms of the current economic situation in our country, this view does not seem acceptable. Our country's economy is backward, and most of the people are poor. Using the silver standard system is still too high a level. If we change to another standard, it will inevitably disrupt finance.

Inspection of Various Countries; Our Country's Currency

Recently, economic experts from Britain, the United States, France, Germany, Japan, and other countries plan to come to China together to investigate our country's monetary system, and divide into domestic and foreign research. The research specialists sent by various countries this time are all erudite scholars who have a thorough study of our country's financial situation. Our country should conduct a systematic study of the current situation of our country's monetary system for the research specialists of various countries, and adopt and implement the results of their research to greatly benefit our country's financial problems.

The Day Before Yesterday's Welcome Rain; Yesterday the Market Stabilized; Rice, Cotton, and Wheat Each Down Three to Five Cents, People's Hearts are Stable; Rainfall is Still Too Little, Hoping for Human Relief

From January to the day before yesterday this year, the rainfall was 13.48 inches, which is 1.67 inches less than last year. Therefore, although there have been several welcome rains, there is still a lack in reality.

Minsheng Paper Mill Case: Litigation Unresolved After Three Years; Zhao Guanqing Appeals, Zheng Yicheng Appears in District Court Yesterday

The Minsheng Paper Mill on Chang'an Road, Zhabei, was originally the property of Zhao Guanqing. Subsequently, in November of the 19th year of the Republic [1930], Zhao leased all the machinery, factory site, and production assets to Ningbo native Zheng Yicheng for operation, renaming it Minsheng Yuji Paper Mill. A lease contract was established. After the January 28th Incident [1932], the Minsheng Mill was destroyed by fire. Subsequently, due to Zheng Yicheng's violation of the lease contract, Zhao initiated litigation in court in May of the 21st year of the Republic [1932], which has continued for three years. Currently, although Zhao Guanqing requested the Shanghai District Court's execution division to auction off Shanghai Paper Mill (where Zheng Yicheng is currently the factory manager), Shanghai Paper Mill's manager Zhang Deming and shareholder Ye Yinshan, among others, filed an objection, so the Jiangsu High Court ordered a stay of the auction. Zhao Guanqing then filed a private prosecution in the Shanghai District Court's criminal division against Zheng Yicheng, Zhang Deming, Ye Yinshan, and others, alleging fraud and damage by Zheng Yicheng and others. The trial resulted in a verdict of not guilty for all three defendants. Zhao Guanqing, dissatisfied with the verdict, within the statutory period, retained three lawyers, Zuo Dedao, Li Mian, and Ye Kuan, to file an appeal, stating that the first defendant, Zheng Yicheng, in his capacity as representative of Minsheng Yuji Paper Mill, should be responsible for returning the factory site to its original condition and compensating for unpaid rent. After the civil judgment became final, during the compulsory execution, the machinery and other items that Zheng Yicheng had moved to the Shanghai Paper Mill were inspected and inventoried. Then, Zheng colluded with the second and third defendants, who came forward and claimed that all the sealed machinery and other items had been sold to Shanghai Paper Mill (the factory they all admitted to jointly operating) by the first defendant in June of the 21st year of the Republic [1932], with the first and third defendants jointly operating it, in an attempt to evade the responsibility of paying off debts. However, it was found that the former Minsheng Yuji Paper Mill was jointly established by the first and second defendants. Although they repeatedly denied it, when Minsheng Yuji Mill contracted with the plaintiff, it was originally stated that Ye Yinshan and Zhang Deming were internally responsible for the share capital, with the first defendant listed as the representative. On this point, not only can Sheng Pihua, the intermediary, and the certifying lawyer Tang Yingsong provide proof, but the judgment to return the factory site to its original condition was issued on May 30th of the 21st year [1932], while the second defendant claimed that the sale occurred in June of the same year. Therefore, according to the judgment, the first defendant, at all costs, concealed assets in order to obstruct creditors, and the first defendant came forward to sign the contract and tried every means to evade responsibility, hoping to stay out of it. Subsequently, he colluded with Zheng Yicheng to delay the execution and assumed a sale of the assets to be executed, intending to conceal them, which clearly constituted the crimes of fraud under Article 363 and concealment of property under Article 384 of the Criminal Code. Yesterday morning at ten o'clock, Criminal Judge Cai Dingcheng specially opened the third court for trial. The defendants Zheng Yicheng and others also retained lawyer Pan Chenge and others to defend them. First, the plaintiff, Zhao Guanqing, and his son Zhao Yangchun, recounted the previous events. Then, Zheng Yicheng testified, stating that he was 37 years old and from Ningbo. He was asked whether Zhang Deming and Ye Yinshan had shares in the Minsheng Mill, and he replied no. He was asked about the Shanghai Mill, and he replied that Zhang Deming was the manager, Ye was a shareholder, and although he was the factory manager of the Shanghai Mill, he actually had no shares. Next, Ye Yinshan testified, stating that he was 32 years old. He was asked whether he and Zhang Deming had shares in the Minsheng Mill, and he replied that neither of them did. He was asked whether Zheng Yicheng was the sole owner, and he replied yes. He was asked whether he knew about the Shanghai Mill buying the Minsheng Mill's machinery, and he replied that he knew a little about it, because the Minsheng Mill was destroyed by fire, and Zhang Deming was a guarantor, so he bought a portion of the machinery. Finally, Zhang Deming testified, stating that he was 41 years old and the manager of the Shanghai Paper Mill. He was asked whether he had shares in the Minsheng Paper Mill, and he replied no. He was asked who the factory manager was, and he replied Zheng Yicheng. At this point, lawyer Zuo Dedao presented the contract agreement to prove that Zhang Deming was the manager of the Minsheng Mill. The judge read it and questioned Zhang Deming about the actual situation. Zhang replied that when the Minsheng Mill was founded, he helped Zheng Yicheng to liaise with various parties, so he was on the scene. The judge considered the testimony and stated that the case required investigation. Lawyer Zuo rose and requested that the defendants be detained to prevent them from fleeing. As a result, the judge ordered Zheng, Zhang, and Ye to provide a reliable shop guarantee to await further instructions.

Rickshaw Pullers Petition the Rickshaw Management Committee Yesterday

Shanghai rickshaw pullers, in order to urge the implementation of new regulations, strictly enforce rent reductions, appropriately limit registration, and implement relief plans, yesterday sent representatives Bian Qingzhong and others to the Public Concession's Rickshaw Management Committee with a petition. Wang Zhisheng received them and promised to discuss and implement it at the next meeting. The main points of the petition are: (1) The rickshaw rental companies, who have been notified from all sides, currently charge between 12, 13, and 14 cents per shift per day. Given the current economic downturn, this should be reduced to 8 cents. (2) New rickshaws are light, fast, and stable, and should be implemented. (3) Military rickshaw registration is capped at 40,000, but recently, at the request of rickshaw rental companies, the quota has been increased by 10,000, and there is a demand for unlimited numbers, which will likely cause future disputes. The number of rickshaw puller registrations should be appropriately limited. (4) The charitable society's collection of donations from rickshaw pullers amounts to approximately 150,000 yuan over ten months. The used accounts should be settled and announced annually. (5) In ten months, the charitable society has only established two locations. More branch societies should be established. (6) Relief for rickshaw pullers should be provided immediately. Especially during this hot summer, registered rickshaw pullers should be given a straw hat, a pair of straw sandals, and a set of clothing, and tea jars should be provided along the roads, and preventative shots for epidemic diseases should be given. (7) The four rickshaw puller propaganda officers employed by the charitable society should be dismissed. (8) Rickshaw puller new villages, bathhouses, children's schools, hospitals, clubs, and other relief plans should be implemented successively. (9) The thirteen new regulations that have been established and publicly announced should be implemented immediately. (10) Do not accept any recommendations or self-recommendations for rickshaw pullers to participate in the board of directors before the general meeting is held.

Shanghai County Government Receives Provincial Order to Complete Unification of Weights and Measures by Year's End

The Shanghai County Government yesterday received an order from the Jiangsu Provincial Government, stating: The unification of weights and measures is the foundation of all construction. All facilities have a direct or indirect relationship with it. All advanced countries in Europe and America have unified weights and measures as a standard. Their scientific development has also largely occurred after the unification of weights and measures. The importance of weights and measures administration is evident. Since the province was ordered to handle it, it has been five years. Many counties have been able to uphold the central government's intentions and promote the unification of weights and measures as scheduled, but there are also many who have taken a wait-and-see attitude, perfunctorily fulfilled their responsibilities, and have not yet completed it. Such procrastination is inappropriate. It is now set that the end of this year will be the deadline for unification throughout the province. Those who are handling unification should pay close attention to checking the work thoroughly in order to achieve thoroughness. Those who have not yet unified should unify according to the deadline and should not delay any longer, causing inconvenience. In addition, the inspection personnel in the unified counties should pay extra attention to the inspection and examination work, and should also be ordered to help handle other construction matters in a timely manner to avoid idleness. In addition to separate orders, this order is issued to the county for compliance.

Relief Society Sent a Large Number of Refugees Back to Their Hometowns Yesterday, Dispersed in Batches by China Merchants and Other Steamships

In recent years, due to severe floods and droughts in various provinces, refugees have been unable to make a living and have come to Shanghai to beg for food. However, the Shanghai market is becoming increasingly depressed, and many factories are laying off employees and reducing wages, resulting in an increasing number of unemployed people. It is difficult to stand. It is reported that yesterday afternoon at about two o'clock, more than 300 refugees, emaciated and with their families, gathered at the entrance of Renji Hall on Yunnan Road, pleading with the Drought Relief Society of various provinces to provide relief. The society believes that the dispersal of a large number of refugees in Shanghai will have a significant impact on the safety of residents, and that providing them with appropriate relief will not be helpful. The society decided to issue each person a free steamship ticket and transport them back to their hometowns in batches on commercial ships of China Merchants Bureau, Dada, Datong, Sanbei, and other companies. The refugees boarded ships at the Xin Kaihe and other docks at the 16th Pier yesterday evening at about eight o'clock, escorted by the society's personnel and the Public Security Bureau's police officers. By eleven o'clock, all the ships had weighed anchor and left Shanghai. It is reported that these refugees are all from the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, including Nanjing, Wuhu, Datong, Yingkou, and Jiangxi.

New York Consul's Telegram Reply Regarding the Post-Mortem Examination of Deceased Sailor He Baosheng; No Wounds, Limbs Not Tightly Bound

The Dagong News Agency reports: Regarding the case of He Baosheng, a sailor on the Lecksiener [Likely a misspelling of a foreign name] steamship, who died under unclear circumstances, the reporter went to various parties to investigate in order to clarify the truth. It is learned that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has received two reports from our country's consul in New York, which have provided sufficient clarity regarding the cause of He Baosheng's death. The details are recorded below:

Suspicious Head

According to the previous report from the New York Consul-General, forwarded from the Overseas Chinese newspaper, the body of He Baosheng was found in the area of Nafu [Likely a misspelling of a foreign name]. Since the general company of the ship was located in Liverpool, an order was immediately issued to the consul stationed in Liverpool to investigate. The consul then replied that after the ship owner of Lecksiener investigated twice after the discovery of He Baosheng's body, there was no suspicion of murder. Later, on April 11th of this year, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegraphed the New York Consul-General to inquire in detail about the circumstances after the discovery of He Baosheng's body. On May 7th, it received a reply from Zhang Zichang, the Deputy Consul of the New York Consulate, who was temporarily in charge of consular affairs, stating that according to the telegram from Dr. Paul J. Parker, the Coroner, on April 11th, when He Baosheng's body was found, it had been eaten by crabs. Because the condition of the head was suspicious, the body was examined. There were no wounds on the outside, or he may have drowned.

Rope Tied on Leg

According to the telegram from the examination enforcer on April 12th, He Baosheng's body was dragged ashore by a well-known small boat. His limbs were not bound, but there was a rope tied on his leg, presumably to drag the body to shore. Later, on the 6th of this month, another report was received from Consul Zhang, stating that the circumstances of He Baosheng's body had been reported. The consulate then sent a letter to the enforcer to ask who was present at the scene when the body was discovered and who witnessed the examination. The reply stated that Cunningham and his son were present at the time and certified that the body's limbs were not bound. There was also a Patterson, who has gone to Filihong [Likely a misspelling of a foreign name]. Because the detailed address was unclear, it was impossible to inquire. In addition, Robin, the current military doctor officer in Washington, was also present at the time.

No Wounds Found During Examination

The consulate immediately sent a letter to the military doctor officer to inquire about the details. On April 28th, the military doctor officer replied, stating that he had examined He Baosheng's body with the coroner on the scene. To the best of his recollection, there were no wounds on the body, and the limbs were not bound. It is reported that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has now sent this report to the Seamen's Union for review. The body of the deceased He Baosheng had no wounds, and the limbs were not bound. The theory of murder is refuted.
