Page 16

Free Talk

Cartoon Material

— Qin Wen

For the sake of "concretization," to depict in detail, and to avoid the suspicion of arbitrariness, literature always emphasizes "description." The drawback of description is that it is troublesome, because the author's opinion can only be implied through "overtones," so a large amount must be written to express the author's intention, which is not as direct and straightforward as "narration."

Although narration is simple and clear, it is abstract and does not give readers as deep an impression as description. It can only be used in unimportant places such as accompanying the main subject. Therefore, literature takes description as its principle, and description should be the main body of a piece.

Compared with painting, the advantage of literature in the use of subject matter is that it is not restricted by time and space. Events that occur in many places and experience many times can be written in one piece. Painting cannot do this. Except for the "Futurist" style, which can slightly extend the time and break the barrier of space, like photography, only the situation at one place in one moment can be expressed in one picture.

However, painting is always based on description. It is also two-dimensional, and the whole picture is clear at a glance, unlike literature, which must be read for a long time to understand its meaning. Moreover, description in painting is easier, especially in comics, which do not require colors and strokes. Just a few lines and outlines can express various moods and make the author's intention clear.

I used to hear about this kind of situation in Chengdu, that is, students take rickshaws, principals take sedan chairs, and teachers walk. Whenever I passed by the school gate around noon or evening, when school was letting out, I always had some thoughts. I thought this situation was very stark, but it could only be used as material for comics and was not suitable for writing a novel. Because if it was just narration, it would be simple, bland, and tasteless; if it was described, it would be very troublesome and not very outstanding. However, using the method of painting, this kind of subject matter is easy to move people and can achieve twice the result with half the effort, so I regarded it as material for comics and did not want to write it into a novel.

This time on the ship, I encountered a similar thing, that is, the writer squats in a corner of the steerage, the bookstore owner sits in a cabin, and the reader lies high in the official cabin on the top deck. I felt that this situation was even more stark than students taking rickshaws, principals taking sedan chairs, and teachers walking, but I also thought it could only be used as comic material. Of course, it is not enough to just show that the writer is squatting in the steerage, the bookstore owner is sitting in a cabin, and the reader is lying high in the official cabin. We must also carefully depict the posture and expression of these three kinds of people; it is multifaceted and complex.

I also think that there is no need to feel sorry for teachers and writers, because some of them also came from such students and readers. Students and readers who take rickshaws and lie high in official cabins, according to the current social situation, will inevitably have to walk on land and squat in a corner of the steerage on the sea in the future when they become teachers and writers. As long as these two kinds of subject matter are drawn appropriately, they will definitely be eye-catching and are indeed good material for comics. However, it is also possible to write them into essays!

The Man-Made Madman (Middle)

— He Luo

His clothes were torn. Tufts of hair fell down, tearing away the scalp, and blood flowed from his nose and mouth.

Mud, blood, and sweat mixed into a filthy sauce.

Such a melee continued day after day. It was as if they were all born fighters, and they could not live without fighting.

Sometimes, the situation of the fight changed. Two or three people joined forces against one person. But the defeated did not give in, lying on the ground for a long time, until their throats were hoarse and they had no strength, they were still fighting.

The mother was the most unlucky one. Whenever her sons fought, the father treated her like a "leaky pitcher," pouring all his anger on her alone, scolding her, beating her, and saying that these were the good sons she had given birth to. These dog-like sons who only knew how to fight.

According to the traditional Chinese spirit, the father was of course right. And the sons had long learned to beat their own wives.

Only the fourth son had not yet married a wife. But it was not because of this that he was more powerful than his brothers: rather, both his father and mother favored him, and from childhood they had cultivated him into a tyrant at home; from childhood he would grab his father's beard, call his father by his name, and laughingly scold his father. The only difference was that now he could run into the street and scold by name, or run on the dirt cliff in front of the yard, and his father could not catch him no matter what.

Although the father did not have as good a face or as good words for him as before, he still favored him in his heart. He only hoped that he would not be so rebellious. And he was always planning for him, and he would definitely give him the best land.

The other brothers resented him.

Everyone wanted to get good land, and to get a little more. Everyone burned with an ugly appetite, and if there was one less person, the property allocated to their own name would be a little richer. And they all opposed the father's plan to allocate marriage expenses to the four brothers.

The father only wanted to punish him a little. But the brothers had higher goals, and they all wanted to drive him out.

The day after they pushed the father down, he came back for lunch and was caught by his brothers without any precautions, tied behind his back with a rope, and tied to the stone roller in front of the main house eaves. He stretched his legs, leaned against the stone steps, and dared not move. If he moved the stone roller, it would roll down and even crush his bones.

The May sun shone on his head, steaming with heat: his shoulders were covered with welts from rattan stripes.

The father, exhausted from beating people, lay on the large kang in the main house, sometimes sitting up, scolding a few words, cursing a few times, and then lying down again.

The brothers all hid in their own rooms, whispering something with their wives and children.

Only the mother was loving, accompanying him sitting on the stone steps, praying to God to teach him to change his mind.

In front of them, scattered broken pieces of bowls, millet, and cornmeal, and several flies.

Sometimes, he shouted, cursed, and declared his unyielding will, his voice full of hatred.

Not long after, the mother secretly untied the rope and let her beloved son go.

II

Where did he go? No one knows.

The father did not want people to mention him.

The brothers only wanted to hear bad news about him.

The mother prayed to God to protect him, to show him a great road in life, and to come back as a good son who could become independent and start a family.

The following spring, he came back. The atmosphere in the family immediately became tense again. The brothers welcomed him with a very fierce quarrel and fight.

He looked at everyone with a more stiff and wild look.

When the father's thought turned to the remote Thousand-Book family of three generations of widows, the brothers were very happy, the mother was also happy, and he was also happy: this was more beneficial, much better than the father's quarter of the property.

The father calculated very carefully that by adopting his son out, he would get more property for himself. The name was obviously to pass on the lineage for others, but the blood was his own, planting his own seeds in other people's fields, the seeds were his own, and the offspring were really his own branch. Moreover, the family business that he had worked hard all his life to create for his children and grandchildren would be divided into three parts, and the share would be even greater.

The father favored him, so the father had promised him the right of inheritance to this unique person and unique business. And according to his own wishes, he was planning and carrying out it with all his heart, teaching him many ways to get close to widows.

After about a year, he and his father finally achieved the goal of plundering property.

But plundering property was not limited to him and his father. In the widow's close relatives, there were also superfluous people who were greedy and lazy, opening their mouths and waiting for food. Now seeing that others had inherited this good property, their eyes turned red with anxiety.

"That Poem"

— Zhou Wen

"That poem I sent (to you) yesterday"—He hadn't even managed to spit out the words "to you" before he realized that using those two words seemed a little too crude. His eyes fixed on her pale cheek and dark hair, and in a flash, his mind ran through a quick revision. Red-faced, he spoke in a more refined tone:

"That poem I sent over yesterday, what did you think?"

Her face flushed as well, even her ears turning a translucent shade of red. Because she remembered that the poem was still tucked inside a book, casually tossed on a table. Ashamed, she slowed her pace a little, raised her face slightly to glance at him, and after her lips twitched twice, she said:

"I'm sorry. I haven't…"

"It's alright, it's alright, it's perfectly alright," he hastily nodded at her, as if he were the one who was deeply apologetic. When he saw her turn her face forward again and keep walking, he furrowed his dark eyebrows, scratched at the oily hair behind his ears, and sighed. "Rats. She still hasn't read it—is she playing dumb? Is she... alas, women!"

He kept close to her heels. Finally, he decided to reach out and take her hand. If she didn't pull away, then it wouldn't matter if she read the poem or not. They would be the same. With that thought, he bent his right hand toward her left, and at the same time, he muttered something vague:

"That poem…"

"Someone's coming!" Her face flushed, and she quickly dodged to the side.

Startled, he looked up and saw two yellow-faced men wearing bird-hunting caps walking toward them. The taller one squeezed his small eyes at him, and the shorter one stuck out his red tongue. Furious, he pursed his lips. But maintaining his composure, he turned his gaze aside and kept walking. However, just as he and she walked abreast of the two men, he immediately heard strange noises coming at them head-on:

"Ahem! Uh, ahem, ahem!"

"Shhh! Shhh! Shhh!"

He saw that she beside him was flushed, and he felt his own cheeks heating up. Avoiding the faces of the two guys, he vaguely measured their build and the back of his own gray flannel suit, and still felt: "Not worth it!" And so, he calmly walked past. Looking at her next to him, she was still looking down, walking even faster, as if she was about to leave him behind. He immediately fixed his eyes longingly on the heels of her high-heeled shoes and took two quick steps to catch up with her. But he still felt apologetic for not protecting her. He almost reached out to touch her shoulder, but he immediately became aware and kept his right hand in his pocket.

"Ahem! Uh, ahem!" seemed to be right behind him.

"Shhh! Shhh!" The tip of his ear seemed to feel the hot breath blowing on it.

He became so angry that his face turned green, and his eyes bulged. But he still kept his composure. He looked up and suddenly saw a white-skinned, high-nosed, black-clothed constable appear at the corner of the street opposite. His left hand was on the black leather gun holster at his waist, and his right hand was swinging as he walked. He could no longer keep calm. He raised his head and turned around, facing the two yellow faces with bird-hunting caps. At that moment, she, who was walking beside him, suddenly covered her suddenly opened lips with a slender finger, and quickly stepped back.

"What are you doing!?" he yelled, green-faced, at the two yellow-faced men with bird-hunting caps. "Hmph, you! This, this, this…"

The shorter one opened his mouth wide, preparing to roar. But the taller one had already seen the high-nosed constable walking up quickly, and quietly tugged at his sleeve. Only then did the shorter one immediately change his lips into an "O" shape and said, "Shhh!" And stuck out his red tongue. The two of them quickly turned around and left.

"What do you think you're doing? Hmph! Absolutely outrageous!" He put his hands on his hips, shrugged his shoulders, as if he was about to step forward.

"Forget it, let them go," she said with a frown from where she stood nearby. But he finally took two steps, paused, snorted through his nostrils, "Hmph, hooligans!" Only then did he turn around, seeming to feel victorious. He raised his head, his face glowing, and walked toward her, making his leather shoes sound especially crisp and loud. He walked up to her.

"Hmph, these things," he said. "If you ignore them, they'll think you're afraid of them! If you don't give them a little taste of what's what, they won't know." As he said this, he stared deeply into her clear, watery eyes, wondering if she admired his bravery. Moreover, he felt as though he had suddenly grown in her eyes.

As they walked side by side, he thought of his plan to take her hand earlier. "After this victory, isn't this a great opportunity?" he thought. And so, in some vague way, he mumbled, "That poem—" and at the same time, his right hand also…

Dreamscape

— You Qi

Turning over,

I think, this must be a dream!

A light gauze veil,

Nets a hardworking heart.

In the distance,

There are mountains, smoking!

Clouds, smoke, mist, obscuring the sun,

Heavy, thick, and long like lead!

Perhaps it is the sea,

A vast expanse, so green, so deep,

Gulls, flying, still calling,

Waves, rolling, pushing and shoving as they run;

No human habitation,

At the end, where the sky and water meet in a line.

A floating boat, a leaf,

A sail, raising tears of bitterness!

Shall we walk towards that line?

Tall figures, holding ropes,

Several shadows, moving around.

A gust of wind rolls up,

The water, smiling foolishly!

Pull faster! Turn the rudder! Use your strength!

Crashing toward…

Waves rolling and running, mouths agape,

The sky and water meeting in a line, that end,

The water smiling foolishly.

University Days (5)

— By German Author Storm, Translated by Chen Yin Zhi

After a while, the pairs of dancers all coordinated. I was the second in the boys' team, and Nali became my dance partner. She smiled when she put her hand in mine. "We have to dance past everyone!" I said—and we did. At first, while learning the "Mazurka," after the first hour, because we didn't dance the whirls well, our old instructor had already knocked on the cymbals with his bow and said: "Miss Bolika! Mr. Fili! You two dance for everyone to see!" As he strummed and sang the song, we danced. Dancing with her did not require any skill, and I believed that no one could go wrong. But the old teacher kept calling "Good!" and the mayor's wife also looked joyful, smiling and leaning on the sofa—she had been sitting there watching very carefully since the beginning of the lesson.

Miss Charlotte was assigned to my friend Fritz as a dance partner. I was glad to see that her lively nature soon made Fritz forget his initial admiration for the tailor's daughter. Now that I had regarded this tailor's daughter as my private property, the beauty and gentleness of my dance partner were what I boasted of. One glance from her neatly dressed rival caught my attention, and following that gaze, I finally realized that the mayor's wife had overlooked one thing: her gloves were too big, not matching her small hands, and were clearly washed ones.

The next morning, when I came back from class, I couldn't be still for a moment. I rushed to the clothes tree, took out my tin piggy bank, and did my best to grope and shake it until I got a silver coin out through the red cloth covering the seam. Then I ran to a store. —"I want to buy white gloves!" I said, with a bit of apprehension.

The clerk looked at my hand with his expert eyes. "Number five!" he said, placing the glove box on the table at the same time. "Let me have number five!" I said softly.

—"Number five? That won't go on," he was already about to measure the glove against my hand.

I blushed. "These gloves are not for me!" I said, feeling more regretful than ever that I didn't have a sister, otherwise I could have put this on her. But now the small gloves with white ribbons were spread out in front of me, and I was very happy to see them. I bought two pairs. Not long after leaving the store, I found a child on the street. "Take this to Nali Bolika!" I said. "Say the gloves for dancing are from the mayor's wife! Come back and tell me what happens; I'll wait for you at the corner."

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

Eradicating Local Tyrants and Evil Gentry Who Prey on the People

— Meng Ruo

This time, in order to eliminate bandits and protect the interests of the people, the General Headquarters has issued a "Revised Ordinance for Punishing Local Tyrants and Evil Gentry in Bandit Suppression Areas." For the class of local tyrants and evil gentry, anyone who (1) acts arbitrarily in the countryside, oppresses the people, (2) relies on wealth and power to deceive government offices or distort right and wrong, coercing officials, (3) flaunts strength and numbers to obstruct government orders or local public interests, (4) borrows the name of the public to levy donations and fees, embezzling wealth for personal gain or occupying public institutions, encroaching on public funds, (5) forges material evidence, directs hooligans to frame good people, (6) protects private opium dens and gambling houses, (7) extorts money from officials under the pretext of drafting corvée labor and public expenses, thereby depriving others of their physical freedom, shall be investigated and dealt with according to law, either with the death penalty or imprisonment. This is truly the good fortune of the villagers in the bandit areas!

Speaking of local tyrants and evil gentry, who doesn't know that they are a kind of unscrupulous elements who prey on the people, relying on their strength and influence? Their behavior can be described as committing all kinds of evil. They occupy a village, like a local emperor, acting lawlessly and demanding whatever they want. Their crimes, as listed in the above ordinance, are still only the major ones. To list their crimes in detail is really not something that a few ordinances can cover. In short, they are simply a heinous demon! The suffering of the general good villagers under their oppression is truly indescribable. However, the villagers, under their tyrannical power, all fear them like tigers and wolves, and can do nothing about them!

In recent years, the anger of the villagers in various places has had no outlet, and thus they have gone astray. Some people believe that this is because the villagers are ignorant and have been incited by others. In fact, there are indeed people who have been incited by others. But those who take risks out of desperation are in the majority. Therefore, to save today's bandit areas, punishing local tyrants and evil gentry is essential.

However, the trampling of villagers by local tyrants and evil gentry in our country is not limited to bandit areas. In all villages, such dregs exist everywhere. Therefore, if we hope that local tyrants and evil gentry will disappear, we should extend this law of punishing local tyrants and evil gentry to the whole country, and carry out a thorough and universal eradication. Unless this is done, it is not enough to talk about protecting the interests of the villagers!

Butcher

— Fang Zhizhong

Village Scene: From the "Grain in Ear" drought to "White Dew," people's eyebrows and eyelashes were scorched, unable to straighten up.

People: After methods of worshiping Bodhisattvas and carrying the "Dog Lord" to pray for rain proved ineffective, the "Plague God" visited them uninvited.

"Good fortune never comes in pairs, but misfortune never comes alone!"

Everyone with a sick person in their family lamented this way.

The plague had eyes; first, it seized the children, making the adults anxious for a while, then it was the adults' turn, one family after another, until it affected the entire village. There was no water to drink, and naturally no medicine to take; the doctors idled, watching this business opportunity slip through their fingers. The discredited Bodhisattvas were even more unlucky—no one went to pray to them anymore.

"It's truly a calamity, Heaven is punishing people!"

Whenever faced with a difficult problem, especially the elderly liked to say it was a "calamity," "the will of Heaven," because no true Son of Heaven had appeared, and people's hearts had become corrupted. Those old scholars who knew a little history would even bring up the story of the "Five Barbarians Uprising" as their argument. Moreover, they sometimes cited examples of emperors when the weather was favorable, the country was prosperous, rice was a few small coins per *sheng*, salt was a few small coins per *jin*, and when someone fell ill, buying medicine and hiring a doctor would only cost a few hundred coins. Now that it was the "end times," everything gave them a chance to reminisce about the bygone "golden age."

Regardless of day or night, the rocket-like wind still bravely swept across, the forest echoed with the desolate melody of late autumn, and the people's hearts and rice paddies alike cracked into pieces, about to fly away.

Although there was no food to eat, no one wanted someone to die in their home. But the disease developed with extraordinary speed, a sign: vomiting, diarrhea, and fever. In less than a couple of hours, the patient would die.

After Li Ba's son behind the mountain died, it wasn't even a day before Li Ba also passed away: but Li Ba was a good person, everyone said so.

At this time, the entire Xu Family Village transitioned from starvation to the terror of death. Whether a patient could be dragged back from the brink of death depended on the merits accumulated by their ancestors and the *feng shui* of their ancestral graves.

Jiang the butcher, around fifty years old, also had a sick son. The butcher's wife, with her rotten peach eyes, constantly complained that in previous years he had used a white knife to go in and a red knife to come out, accumulating countless sins, which were now being visited upon their son. With only one child in two generations, this single root could not be saved; her fate was bad, she hadn't cultivated virtue in her past life, and now it was too late to repent, but she was confident that she hadn't done anything evil in this life. If her son died, it must be because her husband had implicated her.

"How is he? The child is so heavy!"

The butcher's wife squatted in front of a bed covered with a patched quilt, testing the temperature of her son's forehead, then fingering her prayer beads, murmuring "Amitabha." At the end of this sound, she was met with the sound of her son defecating: *splatter*—the three-year-old son had defecated on the bed. The butcher's wife didn't have time to grab a dung bucket and screamed.

"Calling on Heaven won't help me! 'A broken oar stump in Dongting Lake,' ghosts won't save you!"

Jiang the butcher stood dumbfounded, truly like a broken oar stump with no way to help, watching the boat drift with the current.

But he kept the news of the death of Li Ba and his son extremely secret from the butcher's wife—this news would only increase her terror. (To be continued)

This house was located in a corner of the mountain in Xu Family Village, the mottled mud walls having more patches than Jiang the butcher's blue cloth jacket and pants. They had lived alone in this tiny corner of the world for three generations. If you looked at Jiang the butcher's solemn personality and shabby appearance, you wouldn't believe that he had once been a pig slaughterer, considered cruel by people, nor would you trust that he had had a smooth and easy life in his youth. But even five years ago, Jiang the butcher was still doing well.

Naturally, he helped people as a farmhand, just like his grandfather and father, but he had a side business—slaughtering pigs. The motivation was: when a man reaches twenty-five, no one will mend his clothes, especially since the responsibility of "single line of descent" had fallen on his shoulders. But thirty-six strings of cash a year wasn't enough to marry a wife and raise children, so he chose this path. On the fifth and eighth days of the month, and the three festivals of the lunar year, or for weddings and funerals, he would ask for leave to do this business. For each pig, in addition to eating and drinking his fill, he could still earn three or four thousand cash and a few *jin* of pig bristles. He had money and was diligent and thrifty in his work, but because the pig slaughterer was believed to be possessed by ghosts, no one was willing to marry their daughter to him.

It wasn't until he was thirty-six that he married the butcher's wife, but he still hadn't had a son by the time he was forty-six. He was anxious, but the butcher's wife blamed it on him:

"It's always the slaughtering, the killing that harms life!"

After all, a son was more important than money, so he decided to stop doing this business and invited several monks to chant repentance at home and buried the knife in the ground.

Sure enough, the following year, the butcher's wife gave birth to a fat son.

"People must do good deeds! As soon as Jiang the butcher put down the knife, he had a son!"

The neighbors all said this.

From pregnancy to childbirth, Jiang the butcher and his wife were as joyous and cherished as if they had picked up a gold nugget from the sand.

The money they had accumulated was spent as their son grew older. Now it was a "dry season," he had lost his job, and his son had fallen ill. Even people with fields and land in Xu Family Village were helpless, and he, who relied on labor to rent land, was naturally even more desperate. He glanced at the child lying on the bed in the dim light under the mud window, and at his wife, who was leaning against the edge of the bed, crying, and then went out to look at the sky.

The sky was still carefree, holding up its fiery umbrella, and even the seedlings in the wind had been cut off. He hoped that the hour would quickly approach dusk, feeling that darkness was slightly better than this cruel light. He paced back and forth in this short, three-room house, as anxious as a lion pacing in a cage. The butcher's wife screamed again from the room:

"Old man! Shenbao has defecated again! His eyes have sunken in, and he's nothing but skin and bones. Even if we can't afford a doctor, we have to get him some rice porridge!"

"Where would we get rice porridge? The whole village can't find any rice, even the tree bark has been eaten. Don't you know that?" Jiang the butcher responded in the main room, hurriedly bringing in the half-eaten bark rake left over from lunch.

"Heavens! It's as hard as iron, how can he eat it!" The old woman stopped his hand: "A father must always be worthy of his son!"

"Are you trying to force me to die?—In this day and age, who can afford to be a father! Who wants to be a father? I'd rather be his son!"

Zheng Tai's wife from behind the mountain brought the news of the death of Li Ba and his son, and also about Chang Mazi's two children, and the wife of the village head's uncle. Each sentence was like a needle pricking at the butcher's wife's heart. She coldly examined her own son, and a strange pain enveloped her entire body.

Dusk finally arrived. Shenbao sank into the depths of his dying moments, only turbid water flowing from his anus, his eyeballs mechanically turning like a foreign doll. The butcher's wife felt for her son's breath, and again recited "Amitabha, Bodhisattva bless Shenbao." Jiang the butcher staggered back and forth in this dark room, as if searching for something. Suddenly,

"There's no air coming from his nose! It's all because you've done too much evil, and it's being visited on him, you've implicated me!" The butcher's wife cried and stamped her feet.

"Who told him to be born into a poor family? Why blame me?—Did I slaughter pigs? Li Ba and his son never slaughtered pigs! ... There are many people who kill, does that mean slaughtering pigs is a sin!"

Saying this, he went to dig up the knife buried in the ground, for what purpose no one knew. (The End)

Granddaughters and Grandsons

The Sun and Others

— Cheng Quan

When my own endless years flow by constantly in darkness, and it seems as if they will flow into exhaustion in darkness forever, how much I envy and love those golden, large, and healthy sunflowers! They are eternally brave and happy; they live solely by relying on the sun—truly, how eagerly they await this warm and bright sun: they always look at him with their eyes, they always follow him and turn their direction; and when the sun goes down, they also lose their joy, lose the courage to live—in the shade, I have seen their drooping heads sighing and contemplating, how aptly expressing the dying of a life—I understood: it is the tragedy of life!

Thus, for my own small soul being imprisoned for a long time on the dark road of life, I often think of the sun, think of the large, golden sunflowers that love to look at the sun. Perhaps they are relatively happier—when the sun goes down, when it is night, when it is cloudy, although the sun has left them, there is no golden light, nor the warmth of spring; yet they can still imagine, can still anticipate, can still hope! On a muddy road of life that is unsuitable for walking, can you also bear to say: is hope merely an empty dream, a dream that cannot represent the happiness of the future?

Moreover, in the world, who can deny the sun, the mother of light and heat. The sun is healthy, it disinfects, every doctor says so, every living being thinks so; it is the nutrient of life! Think about it: in the arena of life, who dares to be a traitor to the sun? Whoever rebels against the sun rebels against life full of strength and health.

The light and smiles that shine in dreams day and night, how beautiful they should be, yet, how mismatched they are with real life. Yes, dreams and reality are separated by an immeasurable distance; in dreams, I seem to live on warm, dry land, with red flowers, green grass, and the golden light of the sun, where the road is smooth, the wind is light, the surroundings are bright and need no groping, and life is always nurtured under the sun.

However, when this sunlit dream is shattered, and I see my own life again, the world has changed beyond belief! It is still a young soul! However, along with it, I bear the cumbersome shackles of life, stepping forward step by step on a muddy, boundless, dark road, where it is difficult to distinguish the pile of stumbling blocks lying in front of the road, and difficult to breathe in a mouthful of uncontaminated air.

Dragging the burden of life day after day, groping in the dark, with no light, no heat. Where the end will be is hard to predict! Perhaps this boundless darkness will engulf an entire lifetime, and the outline of the sun can only be imitated in dreams forever?—The road of life is the Arctic Circle of the human world, with only mountains and barren land of ice and snow year after year, where the sun is treated as a rare miracle that is not easily seen!

But, can it really be said that the flowers of life can grow in areas lacking the sun? Who can believe this? In any flower, except for poisonous mushrooms, none can survive without sunlight, so how can the flowers of life be an exception?

Carrying life day by day on the road of time, in my heart I deeply remember the sun, the mother of light and heat; but, how far is she separated from me?

Then let the sun disappear forever, let the flowers of life wither!

Movie News

A King's Meddling in Politics

— Nanjing Screening

Jincheng Also Has to Install Air Conditioning

The first-run cinemas in Shanghai mostly screen foreign films. Currently, Jincheng and Xinguang are the two cinemas that screen domestic films. However, Xinguang sometimes still screens foreign films, so to be stricter, only Jincheng is truly a cinema that specializes in domestic films. Therefore, Jincheng Cinema has become the only place for domestic film fans to relax.

In Shanghai, the momentum of domestic films is not as great as that of foreign films. Based on the current situation, it is not that domestic films are not popular, but because their production is too small. For example, Jincheng Grand Theater initially only screened films from Lianhua Company, and it is said that they often felt a shortage of films. However, because they adhered to the purpose of "promoting domestic films," now, in addition to Lianhua, the productions of Yihua, Diantong, Tianyi, New Era, and Jixing companies have been screened in the theater, and the "Dizzy Madness" produced by Yueming Company will also be screened after "The Beginning of Man."

The summer season has arrived, and most cinemas with air conditioning have already opened it. Jincheng Grand Theater already had air conditioning installed last summer, but it was not very satisfactory. It is said that this year the theater has sacrificed a huge sum of money and invited York Company, the most reputable air conditioning expert in Shanghai, to retrofit a new type of air conditioning equipment, which will be completed soon. The air conditioning equipment of the largest cinemas in Shanghai, such as Nanjing Guotai, are all installed by York, and the results are well-known. Therefore, it is beyond doubt that the air conditioning at Jincheng this year will satisfy the audience, and movie fans throughout Shanghai do not have to worry about not having good domestic films to enjoy this summer.

Shenbao Architecture Weekly

The Design of Warehouse Construction

— Little Ang

In recent years, with the promotion of responsible transportation by railways across the country, the rural economy has indeed become much more vibrant. Recently, major shipping companies, such as China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and Sanbei Shipping, have also implemented through transport. As a result, the transportation of goods throughout the country has indeed become much more convenient. However, there are often times when wagons are lacking and goods cannot be transported. Therefore, goods must have a place to be stored, so the construction of warehouses is most needed. In the past, my country's railway freight was not very developed, so the construction of storage facilities was very careless. Even the warehouses of steamships in various ports along the Yangtze River were very simple. These should be specially improved to meet the needs. I will now talk about the main points of setting up warehouses.

(1) Location Selection: Warehouses are divided into two types, one is railway warehouses and the other is shipping warehouses. The key to choosing a location is convenient transportation and easy loading and unloading. Therefore, the location of the warehouse must be built near railways, rivers, or roads. The cargo depot on Maigen Road in Shanghai is in a good location, facing Suzhou Creek in front, backing onto the railway, and connected to the road. Therefore, freight transportation on both routes is particularly developed. Warehouses are generally about ten to fifteen meters away from waterways, and should be within twenty meters of freight stations and roads, because the closer, the more labor-saving and economical. The construction of warehouses should not be too small or too large. If it is too small, it is not enough to store goods, and if it is too large, the construction cost will definitely be very high. Generally, it starts with the current needs, and when choosing a location, one must consider future needs, so the land may as well be larger.

(2) Construction Key Points: Since the size of the warehouse is determined by the amount of freight, its length should be at least fifty meters and at most one hundred meters. Its width is generally fifteen meters. If one warehouse is not enough, several more can be built, some are parallel, some are side-by-side, and some are side-by-side and parallel, entirely depending on the size and shape of the land. However, the distance between each row should be at least fifteen meters, because fire prevention is something to pay attention to. Among the warehouse styles, single-story buildings are the most common, and two- or three-story buildings are the least common.

(3) Material Selection: The key to a warehouse is that it is strong, free from fire hazards, and resistant to rain erosion, so the selection of materials is the most important. It is very good to use copper and iron to build, but it is too expensive. Steel-reinforced concrete is better than any material, and many warehouses have been built with it. Wood is very expensive in China, and at the same time it is not strong and is afraid of water and fire, so remember not to use it.

(4) Warehouse Equipment: Since warehouses are used for storing goods, the internal equipment should be particularly complete. Ordinary warehouses have refrigeration equipment, so fruits, milk, meat, and the like will not spoil. The second important piece of equipment is fire prevention. The fire prevention equipment in Chinese warehouses is extremely careless, so fires are often heard of, and the losses cannot be counted. The third piece of equipment is to prevent moisture erosion. If cotton and agricultural products are exposed to moisture, they will rot immediately, and those responsible for transportation will suffer greatly. These are all extremely important issues, and also extremely small issues. Designers have to pay attention to them. China's transportation industry is still in its infancy. The construction of warehouses will definitely increase day by day, so let the architects study it.

Lighting Design in New-Style Architecture

— Xihao

The importance of "light" to the human body is already well known. It can control people's health, and at the same time, it can affect work efficiency. A building with insufficient light loses the value of the entire building.

There are only two sources of "light," namely sunlight and artificial light. The design of sunlight in architecture is very simple. Just carefully select the orientation of the building and open appropriate window areas on the building to achieve good results. However, the design of artificial light is not so simple. It has a very close relationship with the reflection, color, and intensity of the light inside the building. At the same time, it has a direct impact on the stimulation of the human spirit and the comfort of health. Therefore, special consideration should be given to it when designing.

The most necessary conditions for "lighting" design can be roughly divided into the following points:

(1) Appropriateness of Light Properties - A certain type of light has a special reflection effect on the specified color, which increases the efficiency of light emission, so we should choose a suitable light to meet our purpose.

(2) Avoid Glare - Glaring light is enough to over-stimulate people's nerves, causing dizziness and damaging health.

(3) Average Light Distribution - Average light distribution makes the light intensity in the entire room equal, and the reflection is average, so things in the room can be easily found.

(4) Shadows Should Be Avoided - Shadows can hinder vision and dim the light, so they should be avoided.

(5) Appropriate Light Level - In each building, because the purpose of use is different, the required light intensity also changes. For example, the reception room needs a stronger light level, the lounge needs a gentler light level, and the bedroom can have a relatively weaker light level. Such differences should be given special attention when designing.

(6) Utilize Indirect Light Transmission - Directing light directly into the eyes will not only prevent you from seeing things in the room, but also cause the pupils to contract, damaging the eyeballs. We should use indirect diffused light. To achieve this goal, the distance of the lights can be placed appropriately, and frosted light bulbs or appropriate reflectors can be used.

The requirements for perfect lighting design have been described above. As for the factors that affect the light reflectance, they can be roughly divided into the following:

(A) Ceiling Color

(B) Wall Color

(C) Room Size and Shape

The colors of the ceiling and walls directly affect the intensity of light reflection. Light colors have a stronger reflectivity, and dark colors have a weaker reflectivity. According to test results, the percentage of reflected light of various colors can be roughly divided into the following: (1) White - 95, (2) Light Red - 80, (3) Light Yellow - 65, (4) Canary Yellow - 56, (5) Grass Green - 50, (6) Black - 10.

Among them, white has the strongest reflectivity and is suitable for use in writing rooms, pattern-making rooms, reception rooms, etc. Light red and canary yellow are most suitable for bedrooms and can achieve extremely gentle beauty.

The size of the room is also related to the amount of light required. According to test results, the most suitable "foot candle" for various buildings can be described as follows:

Type Foot Candle

Reading Room 8-12

Pattern-Making Room 15-20

Writing Room 8-12

Bedroom 5-6

Lounge 8-10

Shop Window 30-100

Before designing the lighting, we should first analyze the size of the room, the interior colors, and the purpose of use, and then configure the appropriate lighting. The effect obtained in this way will definitely be very satisfactory.

Recent Portrait of Architect Fan Wenzhao Attending the International Architectural Conference

Architect Fan Wenzhao, under the order of the Ministry of Interior, will attend the International Architectural Conference held in London on July 15th of this year. He set sail on the Empress of Canada the day before yesterday. Mr. Fan departed from the Xinguang Wharf at 4 pm on the 16th to board the ship. Dozens of his relatives and friends went to see him off. It is said that in addition to attending the above-mentioned conference and going to Rome to attend the International Architectural Conference organized by architects from various countries, he will also take the opportunity to inspect the aviation construction industry in various European countries.

(Note) Mr. Fan is one of the leading figures in China's architectural circle. He graduated from the Architecture Department of the University of Pennsylvania in the United States. He is the initiator of the Chinese Institute of Architects in this area, and served as the first president of the association, as well as a member of the Capital Design Committee, a specialist member and standing committee member of the Capital Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum Planning Committee, and a technical specialist of the Ministry of Railways of the National Government.

Architectural Jargon (16)

— Mei Zhenhuan

Transgressing the Boundary - The work done in the construction site, no matter how small and detailed or how large and "strange," must follow the drawings made by the "ghost drawer" (detailed earlier) step by step as the standard, and must not be arbitrarily made up. However, in some places, the dimensions on the original drawings sometimes do not match the location of the foundation. For example, the width of an alley on the original drawing is twelve feet. But after the lime plastering (detailed earlier), because the dimensions of the land on both sides of the houses are accurately calculated, the dimension of the alley is only ten feet or eleven feet. In that case, the dimensions of the drawing and the original foundation clearly do not match. The responsibility, of course, lies with the ghost drawer. Such a situation is called "transgressing the boundary". The two words "transgressing the boundary," like "Kouya Kou Chong Xie" (detailed earlier), have become specialized terms in the construction site. (In fact, it is a verb)

Road Crown - It is the center of the road, because the road slopes on both sides, only the center of the road (i.e., the road crown), and the curb of the sidewalk are at the same height. However, it is best to use the curb as the standard height for the foundation of the house, as it is more reliable.

Nail Driving - When laying floorboards, in addition to using iron horses (detailed earlier) to tighten the floorboards, use wire nails to nail the floorboards in place. However, the wire nails must not be exposed on the surface. (Because after the floorboards are laid, they must be planed smooth.) Fearing that the nails will come into contact with the planer, the nails are driven down with a nail set. It is pointed at one end and about the same size as the nail head. (To be continued)

Comparison of Steel and Wood Construction and Future Trends (Part 1)

— Xihao

In recent years, due to the development of the steel industry and the strength of steel itself, almost all larger buildings have mostly adopted steel as a building material, such as reinforced concrete and composite steel frames, etc., which are now almost universal. Living in this steel world, the wood construction knowledge inherited from thousands of years ago is obviously showing signs of wavering. According to the speculation of ordinary people, in the near future, this kind of wood construction is expected to be rejected by steel construction. But this speculation is absolutely wrong. The use of wood in construction will never diminish. Now let us briefly analyze their properties, and everything will become clear.

The main reasons why wood has been regarded as an important building material by past and present generations can be roughly divided into the following:

(1) Low Price - Several times cheaper than steel or iron.

(2) Very Light Weight - Lighter than any building material.

(3) Convenient Transportation or Handling - Due to its light weight.

(4) Easy to Work With - Can be sawn or cut into any shape.

From the above advantages, we can imagine the low price, lightness, and design convenience of wood construction. Therefore, wood is really the most suitable for general light and temporary construction. Moreover, wood construction has one of the greatest advantages, which is the absorption of vibration. This point is really very important for people's comfort.

As for the shortcomings of wood construction, they are certainly unavoidable. The following are probably the most important.

(1) Easy to Catch Fire - This is a problem with the wood itself.

(2) Defects in Wood - Almost every piece of wood has unavoidable defects, such as cracks, impure fibers, etc. - These defects are enough to hinder the wood itself and the strength of the entire building.
